                                    </b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8/figures/5" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41477-017-0067-8/MediaObjects/41477_2017_67_Fig5_HTML.jpg?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-5-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41477-017-0067-8/MediaObjects/41477_2017_67_Fig5_HTML.jpg" alt="figure5" loading="lazy" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-5-desc"><p>Different types of molecular markers, including RFLPs, SSRs and SNPs, were anchored to the genome. By utilizing this integrated genetic map, previously detected genes and QTLs were accurately located on chromosome 1D. The complete information for all seven chromosomes is illustrated in Supplementary Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#MOESM4">26</a>–<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#MOESM7">29.</a>
                                    </p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8/figures/5" data-track-dest="link:Figure5 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div>
                        </div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec6" data-title="Conclusions"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec6-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec6">Conclusions</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec6-content"><p>We used highly efficient sequencing and assembly techniques to construct a high-quality reference genome for the TE-rich species <i>Ae. tauschii</i>. Our assembly has a scaffold N50 value of 13.1 Mb, and 92.5% of the scaffolds were anchored to chromosomes. We also developed a recombination map and anchored 97.9% of genes and 94.7% of pseudogenes and, impressively, 94.1% of TEs. We discovered a new, Triticeae-specific CACTA family, namely Aet-CACTA-4, which contains 19 subfamilies. The physical distribution of Aet-CACTA-4 is distinct from the other three known CACTA subfamilies. The <i>Ae. tauschii</i> genome has the largest number of pseudogenes among all examined genomes, which may be attributable to historical bursts of TE activity. About half of the <i>Ae. tauschii</i> genes have TE insertions, and bisulfite and transcriptome sequencing revealed that these genes had both elevated methylation levels and reduced transcription. We mapped all of the genetic markers from wheat studies spanning three decades, and constructed the first accurate integrated genetic–physical map of <i>Ae. tauschii</i>. We used these tools to map almost all of the previously detected agronomically important genes/QTLs to chromosomes. These resources should contribute immediately to advancing molecular breeding programmes and disease resistance initiatives, and will facilitate the basic functional characterization of many important and long-sought wheat genes.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec7" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec7-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec7">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec7-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">Genome sequencing</h3><p>The genomic DNA of <i>Ae. tauschii</i> AL8/78 was used to construct multiple types of libraries, including short insert size (450 bp) libraries, mate-paired (2 kb, 5 kb, 8 kb, 20 kb and 40 kb) libraries and PacBio SMRT Cell libraries. For the 450 bp short inserts, the library was sequenced on an Illumina HisSeq2500 instrument with 250 bp per end. In total, we produced over 778 Gb of short read sequences (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#MOESM1">1</a>). PacBio SMRT Cell libraries were sequenced with a PacBio RS II instrument; over 53 Gb of raw data were obtained. No statistical methods were used to predetermine sample size. The experiments were not randomized. The investigators were not blinded to allocation during experiments and outcome assessment.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec9">Genome assembly and evaluation</h3><p>The genome was assembled using the software package DeNovoMAGIC2 (NRGene, Nes Ziona, Israel)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Lu, F. et al. High-resolution genetic mapping of maize pan-genome sequence anchors. Nat. Commun. &#xA;                           6, 6914 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2238">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Avni, R. et al. Wild emmer genome architecture and diversity elucidate wheat evolution and domestication. Science &#xA;                           357, 93–97 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2241">12</a></sup> software (Supplementary Information <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#MOESM1">2.2</a>), which is a DeBruijn graph-based assembler designed to efficiently extract the underlying information from raw reads to solve the complexity of the DeBruijn graph because of genome repetitiveness. Sequencing data from the PCR-Free library and the Nextera MP libraries were used for DeNovoMAGIC2 assembly. PCR duplicates, an Illumina adaptor (AGATCGGAAGAGC), and Nextera linkers (for MP libraries) were removed from the raw sequencing data. Overlapping reads from the PE 450 bp 2 × 250 bp libraries were then merged with a minimal required overlap of 10 bp to create the stitched reads. Following these pre-processing steps, merged PE reads were scanned to detect and filter reads with putative sequencing errors (reads containing a sub-sequence that does not reappear several times in other reads). The first step of the DeNovoMAGIC2 assembly algorithm consists of building a De Bruijn graph (kmer = 191 bp) of contigs from the overlapping PE reads. Next, PE reads are used to find reliable paths in the graph between contigs for repeat resolving and contig extension. Later, contigs are linked into scaffolds with PE and MP information, estimating gaps between the contigs according to the distance of PE and MP links. A final fill gap step uses PE and MP links, as well as De Bruijn graph information, to detect a unique path connecting the gap edges.</p><p>Mate-paired data (20 kb, 40 kb) were mapped to the basic assembly using bowtie (<a href="http://bowtie-bio.sourceforge.net/index.shtml">http://bowtie-bio.sourceforge.net/index.shtml</a>), and only unique mapping reads were retained. Further scaffolding was performed by SSPACE (<a href="https://www.baseclear.com/genomics/bioinformatics/basetools/SSPACE">https://www.baseclear.com/genomics/bioinformatics/basetools/SSPACE</a>, V3.0). PBJelly (<a href="http://www.winsite.com/Home-Education/Science/PBJelly/">http://www.winsite.com/Home-Education/Science/PBJelly/</a>) was used to fill gaps using approximately 10X of SMRT sequencing data. We generated an F<sub>2</sub> mapping population of 490 individuals derived from a cross between the <i>Ae</i>. <i>tauschi</i>i accessions Y2280 and AL8/78. The F<sub>2</sub> individuals were grouped using JoinMap4.0 and then ordered using MSTmap. Finally, using the <i>kosamb</i>i function, we generated a high-resolution genetic map, which includes 164,872 SNPs developed by restriction site-associated DNA (RAD) tag sequencing technology; the total length is 1,153.58 cM<sup>16</sup>. The high-density genetic map was used to anchor the scaffolds to chromosomes using BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Altschul, S. F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E. W. &amp; Lipman, D. J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. &#xA;                           215, 403–410 (1990)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2288">44</a></sup>. The completeness of gene regions of our assembly was evaluated using both CEGMA (Core Eukaryotic Gene Mapping Approach, <a href="http://korflab.ucdavis.edu/datasets/cegma/">http://korflab.ucdavis.edu/datasets/cegma/</a>) and BUSCO (Benchmarking Universal Single-Copy Orthologs, <a href="http://busco.ezlab.org/">http://busco.ezlab.org/</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec10">Genome annotation</h3><p>Protein-coding region identification and gene prediction were conducted using a combination of homology-based prediction, <i>de novo</i> prediction, and transcriptome-based prediction methods. Protein sequences from nine plant genomes (<i>B. distachyon, S. bicolor, O. sativa, Zea mays, Hordeum vulgare</i>, <i>Triticum</i> 
                           <i>aestivum, T. urartu, Setaria italic</i> and <i>Panicum virgatum</i>) were downloaded from Ensemble (Release 33) and were aligned to the <i>Ae. tauschii</i> assembly using TblastN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Altschul, S. F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E. W. &amp; Lipman, D. J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. &#xA;                           215, 403–410 (1990)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2334">44</a></sup> with an E-value cut-off of 1 × 10<sup>−5</sup>. The BLAST hits were conjoined using Solar software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Yu, X. J., Zheng, H. K., Wang, J., Wang, W. &amp; Su, B. Detecting lineage-specific adaptive evolution of brain-expressed genes in human using rhesus macaque as outgroup. Genomics &#xA;                           88, 745–751 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2340">45</a></sup>. GeneWise (<a href="https://www.ebi.ac.uk/Tools/psa/genewise">https://www.ebi.ac.uk/Tools/psa/genewise</a>) was used to predict the exact gene structure of the corresponding genomic regions for each BLAST hit. A collection of wheat FLcDNAs (16,807 sequences) were directly mapped to the <i>Ae. tauschii</i> genome and assembled by PASA (<a href="http://pasapipeline.github.io/">http://pasapipeline.github.io/</a>). Five <i>ab initio</i> gene prediction programs, Augustus (<a href="http://augustus.gobics.de/">http://augustus.gobics.de/</a>, version 2.5.5), Genscan (<a href="http://genes.mit.edu/GENSCAN.html">http://genes.mit.edu/GENSCAN.html</a>, version 1.0), GlimmerHMM (<a href="http://ccb.jhu.edu/software/glimmerhmm/">http://ccb.jhu.edu/software/glimmerhmm/</a>, version 3.0.1), Geneid (<a href="http://genome.crg.es/software/geneid/">http://genome.crg.es/software/geneid/</a>) and SNAP (<a href="http://korflab.ucdavis.edu/software.html">http://korflab.ucdavis.edu/software.html</a>), were used to predict coding regions in the repeat-masked genome. RNA-seq data were mapped to the assembly using Tophat (<a href="http://ccb.jhu.edu/software/tophat/index.shtml">http://ccb.jhu.edu/software/tophat/index.shtml</a>, version 2.0.8). Cufflinks (<a href="http://cole-trapnell-lab.github.io/cufflinks/">http://cole-trapnell-lab.github.io/cufflinks/</a>, version 2.1.1) was then used to assemble the transcripts into gene models. Functional annotation of protein-coding genes was achieved using BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Altschul, S. F. et al. Gapped BLAST and PSI-BLAST: a new generation of protein database search programs. Nucl. Acids Res. &#xA;                           25, 3389–3402 (1997)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2415">46</a></sup> (E-value 1 × 10<sup>−5</sup>) against two integrated protein sequence databases: SwissProt (<a href="http://web.expasy.org/docs/swiss-prot_guideline.html">http://web.expasy.org/docs/swiss-prot_guideline.html</a>) and NR. Protein domains were annotated by searching against the InterPro (<a href="http://www.ebi.ac.uk/interpro/">http://www.ebi.ac.uk/interpro/</a>, V32.0) and Pfam databases (<a href="http://pfam.xfam.org/">http://pfam.xfam.org/</a>, V27.0), using InterProScan (V4.8) and HMMER (<a href="http://www.hmmer.org/">http://www.hmmer.org/</a>, V3.1), respectively. The Gene Ontology (GO, <a href="http://www.geneontology.org/page/go-database">http://www.geneontology.org/page/go-database</a>) terms for each gene were obtained from the corresponding InterPro or Pfam entry. The pathways in which the genes might be involved were assigned by BLAST against the KEGG database (<a href="http://www.kegg.jp/kegg/kegg1.html">http://www.kegg.jp/kegg/kegg1.html</a>, release 53), with an E-value cut-off of 1 × 10<sup>−5</sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec11">RNA sequencing and analysis</h3><p>To aid with gene annotation and to address many biological questions using gene expression level information, we produced a total of 53.21 Gb of RNA-seq data from eight different organs, including pistil, root, young seed, young spikes, young stamen, stem, young leaf and sheath. For this RNA-seq analysis, detailed information about treatment of plant material and experimental process has been described in the literature previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Jia, J. et al. Aegilops tauschii draft genome sequence reveals a gene repertoire for wheat adaptation. Nature &#xA;                           496, 91–95 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2474">16</a></sup>. RNA-seq data were mapped to the genome using Tophat (version 2.0.8). Only the aligned reads located within 600 bp of each other were defined as concordantly mapped pairs; these were used in the downstream quantification analysis. The minimum and maximum intron length was set to 5 bp and 50,000 bp respectively. All other parameters were set to the default values. cufflinks30 (version 2.1.1) (<a href="http://cufflinks.cbcb.umd.edu/">http://cufflinks.cbcb.umd.edu/</a>) was then used to estimate the expression level for each gene based on reads that have been uniquely mapped to the genome. An ‘expressed gene’ was defined as a gene with RPKM &gt; 1 in leaf or root organs of 3-week-old seedlings. The remaining genes were defined as ‘non-expressed genes’.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec12">TE analysis</h3><p>We studied the evolutionary relationships of two class I and five class II TEs by genome-wide identification of RT/DDE domains; we then constructed phylogenetic trees. To identify RT and DDE domains, we first searched known representative RT/DDE sequences against the assembly using TBLASTN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Altschul, S. F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E. W. &amp; Lipman, D. J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. &#xA;                           215, 403–410 (1990)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2494">44</a></sup> and extracted all regions of E-value less than 1 × 10<sup>−10</sup>, and then excluded overlapping hits and retained regions for which the size ≥ 50% of representative sequences. Known representative sequences for DDE domains were from Yuan and Wessler<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Yuan, Y. W. &amp; Wessler, S. R. The catalytic domain of all eukaryotic cut-and-paste transposase superfamilies. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA &#xA;                           108, 7884–7889 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2500">47</a></sup>, and representative sequences for RT domains were from an in-house plant TE database. A total of 100,879 domain regions were identified.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec13">Giemsa-C banding and fluorescence <i>in situ</i> hybridization (FISH)</h3><p>Chromosome preparation from <i>Ae. tauschii</i> accession AL8/78 root tips was performed as described by Han et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Han, F., Lamb, J. C. &amp; Birchler, J. A. High frequency of centromere inactivation resulting in stable dicentric chromosomes of maize. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA &#xA;                           103, 3238–3243 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2519">48</a></sup>. The chromosome Giemsa-C banding procedure followed Gill et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Gill, B. S., Friebe, B. &amp; Endo, T. R. Standard karyotype and nomenclature system for description of chromosome bands and structural aberrations in wheat (Triticum aestivum). Genome &#xA;                           34, 830–839 (1991)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2523">49</a></sup>. Sequential fluorescence <i>in situ</i> hybridization (FISH) with synthesized labelled oligonucleotide probes Oligo-pSc119.2 and Oligo-pTa535 was performed as described by Tang et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Tang, Z., Yang, Z. &amp; Fu, S. Oligonucleotides replacing the roles of repetitive sequences pAs1, pSc119.2, pTa-535, pTa71, CCS1, and pAWRC.1 for FISH analysis. J. Appl. Genet. &#xA;                           55, 313–318 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2530">50</a></sup>. Images were captured with an Olympus BX-51 microscope equipped with a DP-70 CCD camera. The karyotype of C-banding and FISH patterns of <i>Ae. tauschii</i> chromosomes were identified according to homoeology with the D genome of wheat<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Gill, B. S., Friebe, B. &amp; Endo, T. R. Standard karyotype and nomenclature system for description of chromosome bands and structural aberrations in wheat (Triticum aestivum). Genome &#xA;                           34, 830–839 (1991)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2538">49</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Whole genome bisulfite sequencing</h3><p>Bisulfite data from Illumina sequencing was aligned to the <i>Ae. tauschii</i> genome using Bismark<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Krueger, F. &amp; Andrews, S. R. Bismark: a flexible aligner and methylation caller for Bisulfite-Seq applications. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           27, 1571–1572 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2553">51</a></sup> (version 0.12.5) with bowtie 2, requiring perfect matches. The mapping-quality was set to 10 to filter the mapping results to obtain unique mapping reads. Bismark extractors were used to identify three types of methylation (CHG, CHH, and CG). The visualization of the methylation results was conducted using deeptools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Ramírez, F., Dündar, F., Diehl, S., Grüning, B. A. &amp; Manke, T. deepTools: a flexible platform for exploring deep-sequencing data. Nucl. Acids Res. &#xA;                           42, 187–191 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2557">52</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">Genome evolutionary analysis</h3><p>Genome structural syntenic analyses were performed with the MCScanx toolkit<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: A toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucl. Acids Res. &#xA;                           40, e49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2569">23</a></sup>. Owing to the large number of recent duplicates found in the wheat D genome, top 20 BLASTP gene pairs were used as inputs for MCScanx to see if their E-value was less than 1 × 10<sup>−5</sup>. Paralogous pairs of sequences were identified from the best reciprocal matches in all-by-all BLASTP searches. For each pair of homologous genes, protein sequences were aligned using CLUSTALW2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Larkin, M. A. et al. Clustal W and Clustal X version 2.0. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           23, 2947–2948 (2007)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2575">53</a></sup>, and nucleotide sequences were then forced to fit the amino acid alignments using PAL2NAL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Suyama, M., Torrents, D. &amp; Bork, P. PAL2NAL: robust conversion of protein sequence alignments into the corresponding codon alignments. Nucl. Acids Res. &#xA;                           34, W609–W612 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2579">54</a></sup>. <i>K</i>
                           <sub>s</sub> values were calculated using the Nei–Gojobori algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Nei, M. &amp; Gojobori, T. Simple methods for estimating the numbers of synonymous and nonsynonymous nucleotide substitutions. Mol. Biol. Evol. &#xA;                           3, 418–426 (1986)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2589">55</a></sup> implemented in the codeml package of PAML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Yang, Z. PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput. Appl. Biosci. &#xA;                           13, 555–556 (1997)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2593">29</a></sup>. Orthogroups, or putative gene families, were constructed using the OrthoMCL method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. &#xA;                           13, 2178–2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d40588e2597">56</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Integrated genetic map and key agronomic genes/QTLs map</h3><p>We collected all of the known sequences for the molecular markers of the D genome that have been generated in the past three decades, among which there were 735 RFLP markers, 3,536 SSR markers and nearly one million SNP markers. We next anchored these markers to the genome by matching marker sequences with the D genome sequences. QTLs located on the D subgenome of common wheat were also mapped to the integrated map based on their flanking marker information. We also anchored agronomically important genes on the D genome by using a similar approach.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Life Sciences Reporting Summary</h3><p>Further information on experimental design and reagents is available in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-017-0067-8#MOESM2">Life Sciences Reporting Summary</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Data availability</h3><p>The genome sequence and the annotation are available from the National Centre for Biotechnology Information (NCBI) as BioProject ID <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/%20PRJNA182898/">PRJNA182898</a>. This Whole Genome Shotgun project is deposited at DDBJ/EMBL/GenBank under accession number AOCO00000000. The version described in this paper is the second version, <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/AOCO02000000">AOCO02000000</a>. The data that support the findings of this study are available from the corresponding author upon request.</p></div></div></section>

data-test="publication-history"><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Received<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time
